فيكون الحكم على السواد بأنه موصوف بالوجود حكم بوحدة الاثنين، إلا أن يقال المراد من كون السواد موصوفا بالوجود أنه موصوف بتلك الموصوفية وحينئذ يعود التقسيم في تلك الموصوفية الثانية، فإما أن يتسلسل وهو محال أو يقتضي فعل الموصوفية وحينئذ بطل قولنا السواد موجود على تقدير كون الماهية غير الموجودية. وأما قولنا السواد معدوم، فإن قولنا وجود السواد عين كونه سواداً كان قولنا السواد ليس وجود جاريا مجرى قولنا السواد ليس سوادا، والموجود ليس بموجود، ومعلوم أنه متناقض. وإن قلنا وجوده زائد عليه توجه الإشكال من ثلاثة أوجه: أحدها: أنه يلزم قيام الوجود الذي هو صفة موجودة بالماهية المعدومة، وهو محال. وثانيها: أن سلب الوجود عن ماهية السواد مثلا لا يمكن ما لم يتميز السواد عن غيره وكل ما يتميز من غيره فله تعين في نفسه، وكل ما له تعين في نفسه فله ثبوت في نفسه، فالسواد لا يمكن سلب الثبوت عنه إلا إذا كان ثابتا في نفسه فيكون حصول الوجود له شرطا في سلب الوجود عنه هذا خلف. فإن قلت: الذي يسلب عنه الوجود موجود في الذهن. قلت: فإذا كان موجودا في الذهن استحال سلب مطلق الوجود عنه لأن الموجود في الذهن أخص من مطلق الوجود فالموجود في الذهن يصدق عليه أنه موجود فلا يصدق عليه حينئذ أنه ليس بموجود وكلامنا الآن يقابل مطلق الوجود لا يقابل وجودا خاصا. وثالثها: أنا استدللنا في مسألة أن المعدوم ليس بشيء على امتناع خلو الماهية عن الوجود وعلى هذا يستحيل الحكم على الماهية بالعدم فظهر أنه ليس لقولنا السواد موجود والسواد معدوم مفهوم محصل، وإذا كان كذلك لم يكن لقولنا السواد إما أن يكون موجودا وإما أن يكون معدوما مفهوم محصل وإذا كان كذلك امتنع التصديق به فضلا عن كون ذلك التصديق بديهيا.
Thus, the judgment that blackness is qualified by existence is a judgment of the unity of the two [blackness and existence], unless it is said that what is meant by 'blackness is qualified by existence' is that it is qualified by that qualification, and then the division returns in that second qualification, so either it leads to an infinite regress, which is impossible, or it necessitates [stopping at] the qualification, and then our statement 'blackness exists' is invalid on the assumption that the quiddity is other than existence. As for our statement 'blackness does not exist', if we say that the existence of blackness is identical to its being blackness, then our statement 'blackness does not exist' runs in the same vein as our statement 'blackness is not blackness', and 'the existent is not existent', and it is known that this is contradictory. And if we say that its existence is additional to it, then the problem arises from three aspects: First, that it necessitates the subsistence of existence, which is an attribute that exists, in a non-existent quiddity, which is impossible. Second, that the negation of existence from the quiddity of blackness, for example, is not possible unless blackness is distinguished from other things, and everything distinguished from others has individuation in itself, and everything that has individuation in itself has affirmation in itself, so blackness cannot have affirmation negated from it unless it is affirmed in itself, so the obtaining of existence for it is a condition for negating existence from it—this is a vicious circle. If you say: That from which existence is negated exists in the mind. I say: If it exists in the mind, then it is impossible to negate absolute existence from it, because existence in the mind is more specific than absolute existence, so existence in the mind is truly described as existent, and then it cannot be truly described as not existent, and our discussion now concerns absolute existence, not specific existence. Third, that we argued in the question 'the non-existent is not a thing' for the impossibility of the quiddity being devoid of existence, and on this basis it is impossible to judge the quiddity as non-existent. So it becomes clear that our statements 'blackness exists' and 'blackness does not exist' have no coherent meaning, and if so, then our statement 'blackness is either existent or non-existent' has no coherent meaning, and if so, then it is impossible to assent to it, let alone that such assent be intuitive.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a dense philosophical argument from Imam Razi's Muhassal. He is demonstrating that the common division of a quiddity (e.g., blackness) into existent or non-existent is incoherent. He begins by considering the statement 'blackness exists'. If we interpret this as blackness being qualified by existence, then either blackness and existence are two distinct things, leading to a judgment of unity of two (which is problematic), or the qualification itself is what is meant, leading to an infinite regress or a halt, both of which are problematic. Therefore, the statement is invalid. Next, he examines 'blackness does not exist'. If existence is identical to blackness, then 'blackness does not exist' becomes 'blackness is not blackness', a contradiction. If existence is additional to blackness, three problems arise: (1) a dependent attribute cannot subsist in a non-existent subject; (2) to negate existence from blackness, blackness must already be distinguished and have affirmation, making existence a precondition for its own negation (a vicious circle); and even if we say the negation applies to a mental existence, then absolute existence cannot be negated since mental existence is a type of existence; (3) from the earlier discussion that the non-existent is not a thing, the quiddity cannot be devoid of existence, so judging it as non-existent is impossible. Hence, both sides of the division have no coherent meaning, undermining the very division itself, let alone it being an intuitive truth.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'blackness does not exist' is a straightforward, coherent statement.
Correction: Razi shows that whether existence is identical or additional, the negation leads to contradictions or logical problems, so the statement lacks coherent meaning.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's second problem, what is required for the negation of existence from blackness?
A) Blackness must be identical to existence.
B) Blackness must be non-existent in the mind.
C) Blackness must already be distinguished and have affirmation.
D) Blackness must be a thing in the external world.

Key Takeaway
Razi systematically shows that both positive and negative predications about a quiddity's existence are incoherent, undermining the very division of quiddities into existent and non-existent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you worry about what might not happen or what you lack, are you not engaging in the very incoherence Razi exposes? Your mind is filled with non-existent possibilities that have no true meaning. Can you commit to turning your attention away from hypothetical non-existents and toward the reality of Allah's existence?
?
Razi shows that quiddity cannot be separated from existence. Consider your own soul: your very being is a sign of Allah's creative act. Do you live as if your existence is accidental or as if it is a direct reflection of Allah's will? How would your day change if you truly believed that your existence is identical to His sustaining act?
?
The passage concludes that the division of things into existent and non-existent is not intuitive. Do you rely on such divisions in your daily judgments, categorizing people as 'successful' or 'unsuccessful', 'good' or 'bad'? Are you sure these categories have coherent meaning? Can you try, starting today, to see every being as a manifestation of existence itself, not as a label?

The Impossibility of Attribution
Razi argues that attribution like 'body is black' is logically impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that statements like 'the body is black' are logically impossible, and how this relates to the nature of attributes and relations.

Core Idea
Attribution between two distinct things is conceptually incoherent.

Razi continues his critique of logical divisions by examining the simple statement 'the body is black'. At first glance, this seems unproblematic, but Razi shows that it leads to deep metaphysical puzzles about how one thing can be attributed to another. This passage dissects the very notion of qualification (al-mawsufiyya) and argues that it cannot be consistently conceived.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Razi starts from a common division (body is black or not) and then problematizes the affirmative part.
2
Identify the two arguments against 'body is black'
Razi gives two reasons: (1) it judges unity of two distinct things, and (2) qualification must be either negative or positive, both leading to absurdity. Trace each argument.
The second argument is detailed: qualification cannot be negative, and if positive, leads to infinite regress.
3
Understand the objection and response
An interlocutor objects that qualification exists only in the mind. Razi responds: if the mind corresponds to reality, the problem persists; if not, mental fictions are irrelevant. Also, qualification is a relation that cannot exist outside the relata.
This reinforces the impossibility of attribution as a real relation.
4
Connect to the larger critique
Reflect on why this matters for the principle of excluded middle: if affirmative attribution is impossible, the only viable option is negative (the body is not black), which the opponents reject.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجسم إما أن يكون أسود وإما أن لا يكون. فنقول من الظاهر أنه لا يمكن التصديق به إلا بعد تصور معنى قولنا الجسم أسود والجسم ليس بأسود. فنقول: إذا قلنا الجسم أسود فهو محال من وجهين. أحدهما: أنه حكم بوحدة الاثنين على ما تقدم تقريره وهو باطل. الثاني: أن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد إما أن يكون وصفا عدميا أو ثبوتيا. الأول محال لأنه نقيض اللاموصوفية وهي وصف سلب ونقيض السلب ثبوت فالموصوفية لا يمكن أن يكون أمرا عدميا. ومحال أيضا أن يكون أمرا ثبوتيا لأنه على هذا التقدير إما أن يكون نفس وجود الجسم والسواد وإما أن يكون مغايرا لهما. والأول محال لأنه ليس كل من عقل وجود الجسم ووجود السواد عقل كون الجسم موصوفا بالسواد. والثاني أيضا محال لأن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد لو كانت صفة زائدة موصوفية الجسم بتلك الصفة زائدة عليها وهو محال فثبت أن موصوفية الشيء بغيره غير معقولة. فإن قلت الموصوفية ثابتة في الذهن دون الخارج. قلت الذهن إن طابق الخارج عاد الإشكال وإلا فلا عبرة به ولأن موصوفية الشيء بالشيء نسبة بينهما والنسبة بين الشيئين يستحيل أن تكون حاصلة في غير هما وإذا كان كذلك كان الحق من هذه المنفصلة هو الجزء السلبي أبدا لا الثبوتي وذلك عندكم باطل. الاعتراض الرابع على قبولنا الشيء إما أن يكون وإما أن لا يكون: سلمنا تصور هذه القضية بأجزائها لا نسلم عدم الواسطة وبيانه من وجهين. الأول: أن مسمى الامتناع إما أن يكون موجودا أو معدوما. فلا ينافي اعتبار الماهية الموصوفة بهذا الامتناع وحدها وتلك الماهية إذا أخذت لا مع هذا الامتناع يمكن أن يلحقها العدم عقلا إنما يستحيل الحكم عليها بالعدم إذا أخذت مع لواحقها المقتضية لوجودها، فظهر أن القول للموجود موجود والسواد مفهوم محصل والقسمة إليهما صادقة صحيحة.
The body is either black or it is not black. We say that it is evident that one cannot assent to this except after conceiving the meaning of our statement 'the body is black' and 'the body is not black'. So we say: When we say 'the body is black', it is impossible from two aspects. One: it is a judgment of the unity of the two [body and blackness] as established earlier, and that is invalid. Two: the qualification of the body by blackness is either a negative attribute or a positive attribute. The first is impossible because it is the opposite of non-qualification, which is a negative attribute, and the opposite of negation is affirmation, so qualification cannot be a negative thing. It is also impossible for it to be a positive thing, because on this assumption it is either identical to the existence of the body and blackness or different from them. The first is impossible because not everyone who conceives the existence of the body and the existence of blackness conceives the body as qualified by blackness. The second is also impossible because if the qualification of the body by blackness were an additional attribute, then the qualification of the body by that attribute would be additional to them [body and blackness], which is impossible. So it is established that the qualification of a thing by another is inconceivable. If you say: Qualification exists in the mind, not in the external. I say: If the mind corresponds to the external, the problem returns; otherwise, no attention is paid to it, and because the qualification of a thing by a thing is a relation between them, and a relation between two things cannot exist in other than them. If so, the truth of this disjunction is always the negative part, not the positive, and that is invalid according to you. The fourth objection to our accepting 'a thing is either existent or non-existent': We grant the conceivability of this proposition with its parts, but we do not grant the absence of a middle term, and its explanation is from two aspects. First: The meaning of impossibility is either existent or non-existent. Then it does not contradict considering the quiddity qualified by this impossibility by itself, and that quiddity, when taken without this impossibility, can be mentally affected by non-existence; it is only impossible to judge it as non-existent when taken with its concomitants that necessitate its existence. So it becomes clear that the statement 'the existent exists' and 'blackness' [in this context] is a coherent concept, and the division into them is true and sound.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage continues Razi's critique of logical divisions. He first examines the statement 'the body is either black or not black'. He argues that this division cannot be accepted without first understanding what it means to say 'the body is black' and 'the body is not black'. Then he shows that 'the body is black' is impossible for two reasons. First, it judges a unity of two distinct things (body and blackness), which is invalid as previously argued. Second, the qualification (being-black) must be either a negative or positive attribute. If negative, it is impossible because the opposite of a negation is affirmation, so qualification cannot be negative. If positive, it is either identical to the existence of body and blackness (but then anyone who conceives body and blackness would conceive the qualification, which is false) or an additional attribute, which would require another qualification ad infinitum. Thus, qualification is inconceivable. If one objects that qualification exists only in the mind, Razi responds that if the mind corresponds to external reality, the problem recurs, and if not, mental fictions have no evidential weight. Moreover, qualification is a relation, which cannot exist outside the relata, so the correct part of the disjunction is always the negative one (i.e., the body is not black), which his opponents reject. Next, he presents the fourth objection against the principle 'a thing is either existent or non-existent'. The objection grants that the proposition is conceivable but denies there is no middle term, giving two aspects. The first aspect explains that 'impossibility' (as a property) is itself either existent or non-existent, and this does not contradict the quiddity considered without that impossibility. The quiddity, taken alone, can be mentally non-existent; it is only impossible when taken with its concomitants that necessitate existence. Therefore, the division into existent and non-existent is sound and the concept of blackness (as a quiddity) is coherent.

Key Terms
الجسم
السواد
الموصوفية
النسبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attribution statements like 'the body is black' are straightforward and unproblematic.
Correction: Razi argues that such statements involve deep logical and metaphysical problems: they either assert an impossible unity, or the qualification itself leads to infinite regress or other absurdities.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi reject the possibility that qualification (mawsufiyya) is a positive attribute identical to the existence of the body and blackness?
A) Because existence is not an attribute.
B) Because not everyone who conceives body and blackness conceives the body as black.
C) Because positive attributes must be separate.
D) Because the body and blackness are not distinct.

Key Takeaway
Attribution of one distinct thing to another is logically incoherent because qualification cannot be a relation without leading to regress or identity puzzles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is Merciful,' do you unconsciously imagine mercy as something added to Allah's essence? How does Razi's argument expose the logical problems with that view? What must you instead affirm about Allah's attributes to avoid these fallacies?
?
Razi shows that any positive attribution between two distinct things leads to an infinite regress or identity puzzle. Reflect on your own statements about God: are you guilty of treating His attributes as separate entities? How does this affect your tawhid? What concrete change in your understanding will you make today?
?
If qualification as a real relation is inconceivable, how should you think about the relationship between God and His creation? Does this argument force you to reconsider how you speak about God's actions? What specific phrase or habit in your speech about God will you correct starting now?

The Fourth Objection to Excluded Middle
Razi presents and responds to the fourth objection against the principle of excluded middle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth objection against the principle of excluded middle, which argues that there can be a middle state when considering a quiddity without its concomitants.

Core Idea
A quiddity without its concomitants can be neither existent nor non-existent.

Razi presents a sophisticated objection to the logical principle that a thing must be either existent or non-existent. The objection grants that the proposition is conceivable but denies that there is no middle term. It uses the notion of quiddity (essence) considered apart from its necessary concomitants.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text for the fourth objection and its translation. Note the structure: the objection begins with 'We grant... but we do not grant...'.
2
Understand the first aspect of the objection
The objection states that 'impossibility' (al-imitina') is itself either existent or non-existent, and this does not prevent considering the quiddity without that impossibility.
This suggests that a quiddity can be considered without its negation (impossibility) and then it can be mentally non-existent.
3
Understand the second aspect
The quiddity taken alone (without its concomitants that necessitate existence) can mentally be non-existent. It is only impossible to judge it as non-existent when taken with those concomitants.
This implies a middle state: the quiddity considered by itself is neither necessarily existent nor necessarily non-existent.
4
Connect to the principle of excluded middle
If the quiddity alone can be mentally non-existent while still being possible in itself, then the division 'existent or non-existent' may not cover all cases, since the quiddity without its concomitants is a valid consideration.
Razi asserts that the division into existent and non-existent is still true and sound, but the objection challenges the absence of a middle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجسم إما أن يكون أسود وإما أن لا يكون. فنقول من الظاهر أنه لا يمكن التصديق به إلا بعد تصور معنى قولنا الجسم أسود والجسم ليس بأسود. فنقول: إذا قلنا الجسم أسود فهو محال من وجهين. أحدهما: أنه حكم بوحدة الاثنين على ما تقدم تقريره وهو باطل. الثاني: أن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد إما أن يكون وصفا عدميا أو ثبوتيا. الأول محال لأنه نقيض اللاموصوفية وهي وصف سلب ونقيض السلب ثبوت فالموصوفية لا يمكن أن يكون أمرا عدميا. ومحال أيضا أن يكون أمرا ثبوتيا لأنه على هذا التقدير إما أن يكون نفس وجود الجسم والسواد وإما أن يكون مغايرا لهما. والأول محال لأنه ليس كل من عقل وجود الجسم ووجود السواد عقل كون الجسم موصوفا بالسواد. والثاني أيضا محال لأن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد لو كانت صفة زائدة موصوفية الجسم بتلك الصفة زائدة عليها وهو محال فثبت أن موصوفية الشيء بغيره غير معقولة. فإن قلت الموصوفية ثابتة في الذهن دون الخارج. قلت الذهن إن طابق الخارج عاد الإشكال وإلا فلا عبرة به ولأن موصوفية الشيء بالشيء نسبة بينهما والنسبة بين الشيئين يستحيل أن تكون حاصلة في غير هما وإذا كان كذلك كان الحق من هذه المنفصلة هو الجزء السلبي أبدا لا الثبوتي وذلك عندكم باطل. الاعتراض الرابع على قبولنا الشيء إما أن يكون وإما أن لا يكون: سلمنا تصور هذه القضية بأجزائها لا نسلم عدم الواسطة وبيانه من وجهين. الأول: أن مسمى الامتناع إما أن يكون موجودا أو معدوما. فلا ينافي اعتبار الماهية الموصوفة بهذا الامتناع وحدها وتلك الماهية إذا أخذت لا مع هذا الامتناع يمكن أن يلحقها العدم عقلا إنما يستحيل الحكم عليها بالعدم إذا أخذت مع لواحقها المقتضية لوجودها، فظهر أن القول للموجود موجود والسواد مفهوم محصل والقسمة إليهما صادقة صحيحة.
The body is either black or it is not black. We say that it is evident that one cannot assent to this except after conceiving the meaning of our statement 'the body is black' and 'the body is not black'. So we say: When we say 'the body is black', it is impossible from two aspects. One: it is a judgment of the unity of the two [body and blackness] as established earlier, and that is invalid. Two: the qualification of the body by blackness is either a negative attribute or a positive attribute. The first is impossible because it is the opposite of non-qualification, which is a negative attribute, and the opposite of negation is affirmation, so qualification cannot be a negative thing. It is also impossible for it to be a positive thing, because on this assumption it is either identical to the existence of the body and blackness or different from them. The first is impossible because not everyone who conceives the existence of the body and the existence of blackness conceives the body as qualified by blackness. The second is also impossible because if the qualification of the body by blackness were an additional attribute, then the qualification of the body by that attribute would be additional to them [body and blackness], which is impossible. So it is established that the qualification of a thing by another is inconceivable. If you say: Qualification exists in the mind, not in the external. I say: If the mind corresponds to the external, the problem returns; otherwise, no attention is paid to it, and because the qualification of a thing by a thing is a relation between them, and a relation between two things cannot exist in other than them. If so, the truth of this disjunction is always the negative part, not the positive, and that is invalid according to you. The fourth objection to our accepting 'a thing is either existent or non-existent': We grant the conceivability of this proposition with its parts, but we do not grant the absence of a middle term, and its explanation is from two aspects. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The principle of excluded middle means there is absolutely no third possibility between existence and non-existence.
Correction: This objection shows that a quiddity considered in itself (without its concomitants) can be mentally conceived as neither existent nor non-existent, suggesting a middle state.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth objection, when can a quiddity be mentally judged as non-existent?
A) Only when it is impossible.
B) When it is taken without its concomitants that necessitate existence.
C) When it is taken together with its concomitants.
D) Never, because everything must exist or not exist.

Key Takeaway
A quiddity considered without its necessitating concomitants can be mentally non-existent, providing a middle ground between existence and non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider something in your life that you believe is impossible to change. According to this lesson, the quiddity of that thing, without its concomitants, can be considered mentally non-existent. How does this challenge your assumption about its permanence? What would it mean to mentally separate it from its causes? Are you willing to reconsider what you thought was fixed?
?
The objection shows that even impossibility itself can be thought of as either existent or non-existent. Has your certainty about what is impossible ever been shaken? What might you be holding as impossible that could actually be possible? What would you need to change in your thinking to accept that?
?
The quiddity without its concomitants can be mentally non-existent. This suggests that our judgments about things depend on what we attach to them. What attachments in your life have led you to judge certain things as necessary when they might not be? How can you separate the essence from the accidental to gain clarity?

The Impossibility of Uniting Opposites in Judgment
Razi presents the first of two arguments against the proposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi considers the judgment 'the body is black' impossible due to uniting two opposites.

Core Idea
A judgment that unites two opposites is inherently false.

Razi begins his argument by stating that a proposition like 'the body is black' requires understanding its meaning before affirmation. He then presents the first reason: such a judgment unites two distinct realities (body and blackness) as one, which is self-contradictory. This lesson unpacks that first proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the opening lines where Razi sets up the problem. Notice the key phrase 'حكم يوحدة الاثنين' (judgment uniting two).
The passage is concise; each word carries weight.
2
Understand the necessity of conceptualization
Razi says affirmation (tasdiq) is impossible without prior conceptualization (tasawwur) of the proposition. Reflect on why this seems obvious but leads to a deeper problem.
3
Grasp the first impossibility argument
The judgment 'the body is black' treats body and blackness as a unity, yet they are two distinct entities. This is a logical contradiction according to Razi.
He references earlier discussion ('on what has already been established').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجسم إما أن يكون أسود وإما أن لا يكون. فنقول من الظاهر أنه لا يمكن التصديق به إلا بعد تصور معنى قولنا الجسم أسود والجسم ليس بأسود . فنقول : إذا قلنا الجسم أسود فهو محال من وجهين. أحدهما : أنه حكم يوحدة الاثنين على ما تقدم تقريره وهو باطل . الثاني : أن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد إما أن يكون وصفا عدميا أو ثبوتيا. الأول محال لأنه نقيض اللاموصوفية وهى وصف سلب ونقيض السلب ثبوت فالموصوفية لا يمكن أن يكون أمرا عدميا (۱) ومحال أيضا أن يكون أمرا ثبوتيا لأنه على هذا التقدير إما أن يكون نفس وجود الجسم والسواد وإما أن يكون مغايرا لهما . والأول محال لأنه ليس كل من يعقل وجود الجسم ووجود السواد يعقل كون الجسم موصوفا بالسواد . والثانى أيضا محال لأن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد لو كانت صفة زائدة موصوفية الجسم بتلك الصفة زائدة عليها وهو محال فثبت أن موصوفية الشيء بغيره غير معقولة (۲) فإن قلت الموصوفية ثابتة فى الذهن دون الخارج. قلت الذهن إن طابق الخارج عاد الإشكال وإلا فلا عبرة به ولأن موصوفية الشيء بالشيء نسبة بينهما والنسبة بين الشيئين يستحيل أن تكون حاصلة في غير هما وإذا كان كذلك كان الحق من هذه المنفصلة هو الجزء السلبي أبدا لا الثبوتى وذلك عندكم باطل (۳)
The body is either black or not. We say: it is apparent that it cannot be affirmed except after understanding the meaning of our saying 'the body is black' and 'the body is not black'. We say: when we say 'the body is black', it is impossible from two aspects. First: it is a judgment uniting two opposites as previously established, and it is false. Second: the being-described (al-mawsūfiyya) of the body by blackness is either a non-existential attribute or an existential one. The first is impossible because its contradiction is the non-being-described (al-lāmawsūfiyya) which is a negative attribute, and the contradiction of negative is positive, so the being-described cannot be a non-existential matter. And it is also impossible for it to be an existential matter because on this supposition it is either the very existence of body and blackness or distinct from them. The first is impossible because not everyone who conceives the existence of body and the existence of blackness conceives the body being described by blackness. The second is also impossible because if the being-described of body by blackness were an extra attribute, the being-described of body by that attribute would be additional to them, which leads to regress, and that is impossible. So it is established that the being-described of a thing by another is inconceivable. If you say: the being-described is established in the mind, not externally. We say: if the mind corresponds to external, the problem returns; otherwise it is invalid. And because the being-described of a thing by a thing is a relation between them, and the relation between two things cannot obtain in other than them. If that is the case, the correct part of this disjunction is always the negative part, not the affirmative, and that is false according to you.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the proposition 'the body is black' is impossible. The author, Imam Razi, presents two reasons. First, such a judgment unites two opposites (the body and blackness as one thing) which is false. Second, the predication (mawsūfiyya) of the body by blackness must be either a non-existential attribute or an existential attribute. If non-existential, it is impossible because its negation is a negative attribute (lāmawsūfiyya) and the negation of a negative is positive, so the predication cannot be non-existential. If existential, it must be either identical to the existence of body and blackness or additional to them. If identical, then conceiving existence of both should suffice for predication, but it does not. If additional, it would require another predication for that additional attribute, leading to infinite regress. Hence predication is inconceivable. An objection is then considered: perhaps predication exists only in the mind. The reply: if the mental corresponds to external, the problem remains; if not, it is irrelevant. Moreover, predication is a relation between two things, and a relation cannot subsist in other than them. Therefore the correct part of the disjunction is the negative side, i.e., the body is not black. This conclusion is false according to the opponent.

Key Terms
موصوفية (being-described)
صفة (attribute)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why is the judgment 'the body is black' impossible from the first perspective?
A) Because it requires prior conceptualization which cannot happen.
B) Because it unites two distinct things (body and blackness) into one judgment, which is false.
C) Because the body cannot be black by nature.
D) Because blackness is a non-existential attribute.

Key Takeaway
The first argument against 'the body is black' is that it incorrectly unites two distinct entities in a single judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What judgment about Allah do you make that might combine two opposites? Will you take time today to conceive each attribute separately before affirming, so your testimony is not built on a false union?
?
When was the last time you affirmed a belief about your faith without fully understanding its meaning, just because it sounded correct? What commitment will you make to seek conception before affirmation?
?
The lesson warns that a judgment uniting opposites is false. Are there relationships in your life where you treat incompatible truths as one? What step will you take this week to separate the truth from the falsehood in your own heart?

The Regress Argument Against Predication as an Extra Attribute
Razi examines the two possibilities for predication and eliminates both.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why predication (mawsūfiyya) cannot be an existential attribute without leading to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
Predication cannot be an extra attribute because it would require a chain of further predications.

After the first reason, Razi provides a detailed second argument focusing on the nature of predication (being-described). He examines whether predication is a non-existential or existential attribute and shows both lead to impossibility. The key insight is that if predication were an existential attribute, it would either be identical to the existence of its terms or additional, and both lead to absurdity, especially infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two possibilities
Read the Arabic text where Razi splits the predication (mawsūfiyya) into non-existential and existential. Follow his reasoning for each branch.
Pay attention to the logical disjunction (إما أن يكون...).
2
Understand why non-existential is impossible
Razi argues that if predication were non-existential, its negation (lāmawsūfiyya) would be a negative attribute, and contradicting a negative yields a positive, so predication cannot be non-existential.
This uses the concept that the negation of a negation is affirmation.
3
Analyze the existential branch
If predication is existential, it is either identical to the existence of body and blackness or distinct. Razi shows both are impossible: identity fails because conceiving existence does not entail conceiving predication; distinctness leads to regress.
The regress argument is crucial: if predication is an extra attribute, then the body's being-described by that attribute is another predication, ad infinitum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجسم إما أن يكون أسود وإما أن لا يكون. فنقول من الظاهر أنه لا يمكن التصديق به إلا بعد تصور معنى قولنا الجسم أسود والجسم ليس بأسود . فنقول : إذا قلنا الجسم أسود فهو محال من وجهين. أحدهما : أنه حكم يوحدة الاثنين على ما تقدم تقريره وهو باطل . الثاني : أن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد إما أن يكون وصفا عدميا أو ثبوتيا. الأول محال لأنه نقيض اللاموصوفية وهى وصف سلب ونقيض السلب ثبوت فالموصوفية لا يمكن أن يكون أمرا عدميا (۱) ومحال أيضا أن يكون أمرا ثبوتيا لأنه على هذا التقدير إما أن يكون نفس وجود الجسم والسواد وإما أن يكون مغايرا لهما . والأول محال لأنه ليس كل من يعقل وجود الجسم ووجود السواد يعقل كون الجسم موصوفا بالسواد . والثانى أيضا محال لأن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد لو كانت صفة زائدة موصوفية الجسم بتلك الصفة زائدة عليها وهو محال فثبت أن موصوفية الشيء بغيره غير معقولة (۲) فإن قلت الموصوفية ثابتة فى الذهن دون الخارج. قلت الذهن إن طابق الخارج عاد الإشكال وإلا فلا عبرة به ولأن موصوفية الشيء بالشيء نسبة بينهما والنسبة بين الشيئين يستحيل أن تكون حاصلة في غير هما وإذا كان كذلك كان الحق من هذه المنفصلة هو الجزء السلبي أبدا لا الثبوتى وذلك عندكم باطل (۳)
The body is either black or not. We say: it is apparent that it cannot be affirmed except after understanding the meaning of our saying 'the body is black' and 'the body is not black'. We say: when we say 'the body is black', it is impossible from two aspects. First: it is a judgment uniting two opposites as previously established, and it is false. Second: the being-described (al-mawsūfiyya) of the body by blackness is either a non-existential attribute or an existential one. The first is impossible because its contradiction is the non-being-described (al-lāmawsūfiyya) which is a negative attribute, and the contradiction of negative is positive, so the being-described cannot be a non-existential matter. And it is also impossible for it to be an existential matter because on this supposition it is either the very existence of body and blackness or distinct from them. The first is impossible because not everyone who conceives the existence of body and the existence of blackness conceives the body being described by blackness. The second is also impossible because if the being-described of body by blackness were an extra attribute, the being-described of body by that attribute would be additional to them, which leads to regress, and that is impossible. So it is established that the being-described of a thing by another is inconceivable. If you say: the being-described is established in the mind, not externally. We say: if the mind corresponds to external, the problem returns; otherwise it is invalid. And because the being-described of a thing by a thing is a relation between them, and the relation between two things cannot obtain in other than them. If that is the case, the correct part of this disjunction is always the negative part, not the affirmative, and that is false according to you.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the proposition 'the body is black' is impossible. The author, Imam Razi, presents two reasons. First, such a judgment unites two opposites (the body and blackness as one thing) which is false. Second, the predication (mawsūfiyya) of the body by blackness must be either a non-existential attribute or an existential attribute. If non-existential, it is impossible because its negation is a negative attribute (lāmawsūfiyya) and the negation of a negative is positive, so the predication cannot be non-existential. If existential, it must be either identical to the existence of body and blackness or additional to them. If identical, then conceiving existence of both should suffice for predication, but it does not. If additional, it would require another predication for that additional attribute, leading to infinite regress. Hence predication is inconceivable. Key Terms
موصوفية (being-described)
عدمي/ثبوتي (non-existential/existential)
نسبة (relation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think predication is a simple relation that does not need further analysis, but Razi shows it leads to logical problems.
Correction: Razi demonstrates that predication cannot be a positive attribute without infinite regress or contradiction.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi reject the idea that predication (mawsūfiyya) is an existential attribute identical to the existence of its terms?
A) Because existence is not an attribute.
B) Because one can conceive body and blackness without conceiving predication.
C) Because it would lead to infinite regress.
D) Because blackness is non-existential.

Key Takeaway
Predication cannot be an existential attribute as it leads either to non-identity or infinite regress, making it inconceivable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a believer,' do you treat 'believer' as a real attribute added to your essence? Razi's argument shows such predication leads to an infinite regress if taken literally. How does this challenge your understanding of self-description?
?
Razi concludes that 'the being-described of a thing by another is inconceivable.' Does this mean you should stop making statements like 'This is a book'? If not, how do you reconcile everyday language with this philosophical conclusion? What alternative understanding of predication can you adopt?
?
This argument forces you to examine the very act of making a claim. Take one belief you hold about yourself—say, 'I am compassionate.' Can you identify a way this predication avoids the regress? If not, what does that imply about the nature of your belief? Will you still make such statements with the same confidence?

The Objection of Mental Existence and the Relation Argument
Razi answers an objection and gives a final argument based on the nature of relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that predication exists only in the mind and Razi's refutation based on the nature of relation.

Core Idea
If predication is mental, it cannot correspond to external reality, and a relation cannot exist outside its relata.

Razi anticipates an objection: perhaps predication (mawsūfiyya) is not in external reality but only in the mind. He replies with two points. First, if the mental representation corresponds to external reality, the same problem recurs; if not, it is irrelevant. Second, predication is a relation between two things, and a relation cannot subsist in something other than its relata. This final blow seals the argument that the judgment 'the body is black' is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and reply
Read the Arabic text starting with 'فإن قلت'. Understand the objection: predication is mental. Then read Razi's reply.
The reply has two parts: correspondence problem and relation argument.
2
Analyze the correspondence point
Razi says if mental predication matches external reality, the earlier problems remain (since it would mirror the same structure). If it does not match, then mental predication is arbitrary and invalid.
3
Understand the relation argument
Predication is a relation (nisba) between body and blackness. A relation cannot exist in a third thing; it must be between the two. Since predication would need a substrate, it is impossible.
This is a metaphysical principle about relations.
4
Conclude the overall argument
Razi concludes that in the disjunction (the body is either black or not), the negative part is always correct according to his analysis, which the opponent would reject.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجسم إما أن يكون أسود وإما أن لا يكون. فنقول من الظاهر أنه لا يمكن التصديق به إلا بعد تصور معنى قولنا الجسم أسود والجسم ليس بأسود . فنقول : إذا قلنا الجسم أسود فهو محال من وجهين. أحدهما : أنه حكم يوحدة الاثنين على ما تقدم تقريره وهو باطل . الثاني : أن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد إما أن يكون وصفا عدميا أو ثبوتيا. الأول محال لأنه نقيض اللاموصوفية وهى وصف سلب ونقيض السلب ثبوت فالموصوفية لا يمكن أن يكون أمرا عدميا (۱) ومحال أيضا أن يكون أمرا ثبوتيا لأنه على هذا التقدير إما أن يكون نفس وجود الجسم والسواد وإما أن يكون مغايرا لهما . والأول محال لأنه ليس كل من يعقل وجود الجسم ووجود السواد يعقل كون الجسم موصوفا بالسواد . والثانى أيضا محال لأن موصوفية الجسم بالسواد لو كانت صفة زائدة موصوفية الجسم بتلك الصفة زائدة عليها وهو محال فثبت أن موصوفية الشيء بغيره غير معقولة (۲) فإن قلت الموصوفية ثابتة فى الذهن دون الخارج. قلت الذهن إن طابق الخارج عاد الإشكال وإلا فلا عبرة به ولأن موصوفية الشيء بالشيء نسبة بينهما والنسبة بين الشيئين يستحيل أن تكون حاصلة في غير هما وإذا كان كذلك كان الحق من هذه المنفصلة هو الجزء السلبي أبدا لا الثبوتى وذلك عندكم باطل (۳)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that predication can exist solely in the mind without external reality, but Razi shows this is problematic.
Correction: Even mental predication leads to problems if it corresponds to reality, and if it does not, it is meaningless. Also, as a relation, it cannot exist in the mind as a separate entity.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's reply, why can't predication (mawsūfiyya) be merely mental?
A) Because the mind cannot conceive relations.
B) Because if the mental corresponds to external, the problem returns; also, a relation cannot exist in a third thing like the mind.
C) Because blackness is not mental.
D) Because the body is external.

Key Takeaway
The objection of mental existence fails because correspondence preserves the problem, and a relation cannot exist in a third subject.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your beliefs about Allah, do you ever settle for a mental concept that you haven't tested against the reality of what revelation teaches? In what area is your understanding merely a comfortable mental construct rather than a truth that shapes your life? Commit to identifying one such belief this week and seeking its external correspondence through the Qur'an and Sunnah.
?
Razi warns that if your mental picture doesn't match external reality, it's irrelevant. Is there a gap between what you claim to believe (externally) and what you actually act upon (mentally)? Write down one specific teaching of aqeedah that you intellectually affirm but have not translated into practice, and outline one concrete action to close that gap.
?
This argument shows that a relation cannot exist in a third thing—it must be directly between the two relata. In your relationship with your Creator, are you relying on intermediaries (habits, scholars, rituals) to define that relationship without cultivating a direct connection? What would it mean for you to personally engage with Allah's attributes without a mental filter of mere routine?
